The organ can be simple, or as complex as the human eye; equipped with lenses, shutters, color filters and reflectors. The light can be produced from compounds during the digestion of prey, from specialized mitochondrial cells in the organism, called photocytes ("light producing" cells) , or, similarly, associated with symbiotic  bacteria in the organism.|

|[ENVO:01000167](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000167)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;determinate root nodule|Determinate nodules are root nodules found on tropical (sub)legumes, such as those of the genera Glycine (soybean), Phaseolus  (common bean), Lotus, and Vigna. Determinate nodules lose meristematic activity shortly after initiation, thus growth is due to cell expansion resulting in mature nodules which are spherical in shape.|
|[ENVO:01000168](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000168)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeterminate root nodule|Indeterminate nodules are found on temperate legumes like Pisum  (pea), Medicago (alfalfa), Trifolium (clover), and Vicia (vetch). They earned the moniker "indeterminate" because they maintain an active apical meristem that produces new cells for growth over the life of the nodule. Because they are actively growing, indeterminate nodules manifest zones which demarcate different stages of development/symbiosis.|
|[ENVO:01000169](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000169)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeterminate root nodule active meristem|A part of an indeterminate root nodule where new nodule tissue is formed which will later differentiate into the other zones of the nodule.|
|[ENVO:01000170](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000170)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeterminate root nodule infection zone|A part of an indeterminate root nodule permeated with infection threads full of bacteria. The plant cells are larger than in the previous zone and cell division is halted.|
|[ENVO:01000171](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000171)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeterminate root nodule nitrogen fixation zone|A part of an indeterminate root nodule where each cell contains a large, central vacuole and the cytoplasm is filled with fully differentiated bacteroids which are actively fixing nitrogen. Typically, the plant provides these cells with leghemoglobin, resulting in a distinct pink color.|
|[ENVO:01000172](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000172)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeterminate root nodule senescent zone|A part of an indeterminate root nodule where plant cells and their bacteroid contents are being degraded. The breakdown of the heme component of leghemoglobin results in a visible greening at the base of the nodule.|

The term may be applied to similar organs in other worms.|
|[ENVO:01000166](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000166)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mycetome|A specialized organ that is linked to the gut in beetles and host to a symbiotic yeast. The yeast cells assist in the digestion of less nutritious foods, supply needed B-vitamins and sterols, and provide resistance to certain toxins.|

|[ENVO:00000167](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000167)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bar|A linear shoaling landform feature within a body of water. Bars tend to be long and narrow (linear) and develop where a current (or waves) promote deposition of granular material, resulting in localized shallowing (shoaling) of the water. Bars can appear in the sea, in a lake, or in a river. They are typically composed of sand, although could be of any granular matter that the moving water has access to and is capable of shifting around (for example, soil, silt, gravel, cobble, shingle, or even boulders). The grain size of the material comprising a bar is related: to the size of the waves or the strength of the currents moving the material, but the availability of material to be worked by waves and currents is also important.|
|[ENVO:00000306](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000306)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;spit|A deposition landform found off coasts. A spit is a type of bar or beach that develops where a re-entrant occurs, such as at a cove, bay, ria, or river mouth. Spits are formed by the movement of sediment (typically sand) along a shore by a process known as longshore drift. Where the direction of the shore turns inland (reenters) the longshore current spreads out or dissipates. No longer able to carry the full load, much of the sediment is dropped. This causes a bar to build out from the shore, eventually becoming a spit.|
|[ENVO:00000420](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000420)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tombolo|A deposition landform such as a spit or bar which forms a narrow piece of land between an island or offshore rock and a mainland shore, or between two islands or offshore rocks. They usually form because the island causes wave refraction, depositing sand and shingle moved by longshore drift in each direction around the island where the waves meet. Eustatic sea level rise may also contribute to accretion as material is pushed up with rising sea levels.|

|[ENVO:00000406](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000406)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mid-ocean ridge|An underwater mountain range, formed by plate tectonics. This uplifting of the ocean floor occurs when convection currents rise in the mantle beneath the oceanic crust and create magma where two tectonic plates meet at a divergent boundary. The mid-ocean ridges of the world are connected and form a single global mid-oceanic ridge system that is part of every ocean.|

|[ENVO:01000067](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000067)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine current|A hydroform which is maintained by a continuous, directed movement of marine water, generated by forces caused by breaking waves, wind, Coriolis force, temperature and salinity differences, and tides caused by the gravitational pull of astronomical bodies. Depth contours, shoreline configurations and interaction with other currents influence a current's direction and strength.|
|[ENVO:00000147](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000147)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ocean current|The region occupied by any more or less continuous, directed movement of ocean water that flows in one of the Earth's oceans. Ocean Currents are rivers of hot or cold water within the ocean. The currents are generated from the forces acting upon the water like the earth's rotation, the wind, the temperature and salinity differences and the gravitation of the moon. The depth contours, the shoreline and other movements influence the direction and strength of the movements of water that forms a given current.|

|[ENVO:00000442](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000442)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;maelstrom|A very powerful whirlpool.|
|[ENVO:01000062](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000062)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine benthic storm|Benthic storms are strong benthic (near bottom) currents transporting sediment, created by the input of energy (largely kinetic) to the seabed. In regions with high mesoscale eddy activity, benthic storms are frequent and can create isohaline and isothermal conditions extending as much as 1000m above the seafloor.|
|[ENVO:01000064](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000064)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine downwelling|A marine downwelling describes a net current of marine surface water towards deeper regions of the water column. Marine downwellings are usually caused by differences in the density (and hence, temperature and salinity) of seawater.|
|[ENVO:01000068](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000068)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine streamer|Marine streamers are tongues of cold water that extend > 100 km offshore from upwelling regions. Enhanced primary productivity may occur in these waters as they are typically more nutrient rich than marine surface waters.|
|[ENVO:01000069](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000069)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mesoscale marine eddy|Mesoscale marine eddies are characterized by currents which flow in a roughly circular motion around the center of the eddy. The sense of rotation of these currents may either be cyclonic or anticyclonic. Ocean eddies are also usually made of water masses that are different to those outside of the eddy. Marine mesoscale eddies are between about 10 and 500 km in diameter, and persist for periods of days to months. They may be formed when an ocean current develops an instability. This instability grows, causing the current to meander, and eventually an eddy is pinched off from the meander.|
|[ENVO:01000074](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000074)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;oceanic gyre|A gyre in oceanography is any large system of rotating ocean currents, particularly those involved with large wind movements. Gyres are caused by the Coriolis Effect; planetary vorticity  along with horizontal and vertical friction, which determine the circulation patterns from the wind curl (torque).|
|[ENVO:01000098](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000098)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deep ocean current|A marine current that generally occurs below the permanent thermocline (where it occurs) or below 400 m depth and that is driven by density and temperature gradients.|
|[ENVO:01000099](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000099)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine surface current|A marine current bordered by the surface of the water column and the permanent thermocline, where it occurs. Surface currents are mostly wind driven and mostly limited to the top 400 m of the water column. Ocean currents are driven by the circulation of wind above surface waters. Frictional stress at the interface between the ocean and the wind causes the water to move in the direction of the wind. Large ocean currents are a response of the atmosphere and ocean to the flow of energy from the tropics to polar regions. In some cases, currents are transient features and affect only a small area. Other ocean currents are essentially permanent and extend over large horizontal distances.|
|[ENVO:01000100](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000100)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;along-front current|A marine surface current that flows along an oceanic front.|
|[ENVO:01000101](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000101)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;warm surface current|warm surface current|
|[ENVO:01000103](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000103)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;western boundary current|A warm water, narrow marine surface current flowing from the equator to high latitudes at speeds between 40 and 120 kilometers per day. Western boundary currents are the deepest ocean surface flows, usually extending 1000 meters below the ocean surface.|
|[ENVO:01000102](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000102)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cold surface current|cold surface current|
|[ENVO:01000104](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000104)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;eastern boundary current|A cold water, broad marine surface current flowing from high latitudes to the equator at speeds between 3 and 7 kilometers per day.|
|[ENVO:01001336](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001336)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine tidal flow|A marine current which is maintained by a tidal flow process.|
|[ENVO:01000075](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000075)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine thermocline|The marine thermocline describes a sharp change in the temperature of seawater (in relation to the temperature gradients of the water mass surrounding it) in the marine water column, which is usually associated with rapid changes in water density and salinity.|
|[ENVO:01000106](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000106)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;permanent marine thermocline|The permanent marine thermocline describes a marine thermocline found in temperate to tropical latitudes, which marks the transition between warm waters and cold deep waters. The permanent thermocline separates the marine cold-water sphere and the marine warm-water sphere|
|[ENVO:01000107](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000107)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;seasonal marine thermocline|The seasonal marine thermocline is a marine thermocline, which generally occurs below the marine wind mixed layer.|
|[ENVO:01000076](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000076)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine chemocline|A marine chemocline is a marine cline caused by a strong, vertical chemistry gradient within a body of marine water. Chemoclines most commonly occur where local conditions favor the formations of anoxic bottom water.|
|[ENVO:01000077](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000077)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine pycnocline|The marine pycnocline describes a sharp change in the density of seawater (in relation to the gradients of the water mass surrounding it) in the marine water column. Pycnoclines are usually associated with thermo- and haloclines.|
|[ENVO:01000078](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000078)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine nutricline|The marine nutricline describes a sharp change in the nutrient content of seawater (in relation to the gradients of the water mass surrounding it) in the marine water column.|
|[ENVO:01000261](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000261)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lysocline|A layer within a marine water body where the rate of calcite dissolution changes rapidly with depth. The increase in the rate of calcite dissolution with depth is largely due to the concomitant fall in calcite saturation.|
|[ENVO:01000079](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000079)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine lysocline|The marine lysocline denotes the depth in the ocean below which the rate of dissolution of calcite increases dramatically. As water column depth and therefore pressure increases, the corresponding calcite saturation of seawater decreases and the calcite begins dissolve.|

|[ENVO:00000210](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000210)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine aphotic zone|The zone of an ocean below 200m, in which photosynthesis cannot occur due to the lack of light.|
|[ENVO:00000211](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000211)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine bathypelagic zone|The one of an ocean below the 10degC thermocline down to a temperature of 4degC.|
|[ENVO:00000212](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000212)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine abyssalpelagic zone|The zone of the ocean below the bathypelagic zone, with its lowest boundary at about 6000m.|
|[ENVO:00000213](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000213)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine mesopelagic zone|The zone of an ocean immediately below the photic zone down to a depth where the water temperature is 10degC (the thermocline).|

It is separated from the marine cold-water sphere by the permanent marine thermocline|

|[ENVO:2000004](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:2000004)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;algal bloom|A feature that arises from a rapid increase or accumulation in the population of algae (typically microscopic) in an aquatic system.|
|[ENVO:01000057](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000057)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine algal bloom|A marine algal bloom is a rapid increase or accumulation in the population of algae in a marine system. Typically, only one or a small number of phytoplankton  species are involved. Although there is no officially recognized threshold level, algae can be considered to be blooming at concentrations of hundreds to thousands of cells per milliliter, depending on the severity.|
|[ENVO:2000005](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:2000005)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;freshwater algal bloom|An algal bloom that is located in freshwater. Freshwater algal blooms are the result of an excess of nutrients, particularly some phosphates.|

|[ENVO:00000215](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000215)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hydrothermal vent|A fissure in the Earths's surface from which geothermally heated water issues.|
|[ENVO:01000122](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000122)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine hydrothermal vent|A marine hydrothermal vent is a marine benthic feature where heat generated due to tectonic activity, either at divergent plate boundaries or convergent ocean plates where back-arc spreading occurs, is released or 'vented' to the surface. The resultant high temperature water jets are laden with dissolved metals and minerals.|
|[ENVO:00000218](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000218)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;black smoker|A hydrothermal vent found on the ocean floor. The vents are formed in fields hundreds of meters wide when superheated water from below the Earth's crust comes through the ocean floor. The superheated water is rich in dissolved minerals from the crust, most notably sulfides, which crystallize to create a chimney-like structure around each vent. When the superheated water in the vent comes in contact with the cold ocean water, many minerals are precipitated, creating the distinctive black color. The metal sulfides that are deposited can become massive sulfide ore deposits in time.|
|[ENVO:01000257](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000257)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;white smoker|A hydrothermal vent found on the ocean floor which emits lighter-hued minerals, such as those containing barium, calcium and silicon. These alkaline hydrothermal vents also continuously generate acetyl thioesters, providing both the starting point for more complex organic molecules and the energy needed to produce them.|
|[ENVO:01000262](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000262)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;seep|A seep is a spring in which water has filtered through permeable earth to the surface.|

This seep has been proposed as an intermediate between cold seeps and hydrothermal vents.|

|[ENVO:00000391](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000391)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;land bridge|An isthmus or other land connection between what at other times are separate land masses which allows animals and plants to cross and colonise new lands. Land bridges are commonly created by regression, in which sea levels fall exposing previously submerged sections of continental shelf. Land bridges are also formed by: (a) upthrust at the edge of continental plates; and (b) glacial retreat alleviating pressure on shallow marine formations.|
|[ENVO:00000177](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000177)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;moraine|An accumulation of boulders, stones, or other debris carried and deposited by a glacier.|
|[ENVO:00000249](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000249)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lateral moraine|The parallel ridges of till deposited along the sides of an alglacier. The unconsolidated debris is deposited on top of the glacier by frost shattering of the valley walls and from tributary streams flowing into the valley. The till is carried along the glacial margin until the glacier melts.|
|[ENVO:00000250](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000250)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;medial moraine|A moriane formed when the inside lateral moraines of two glaciers merge together. They form a ridge down the center of the combined glaciers.|
|[ENVO:00000251](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000251)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ground moraine|A till covered area with irregular topography and no ridges, often forming gently rolling hills or plains. Forms by the accumulation of till under the ice by lodgement, but may also be deposited as the glacier retreats.|
|[ENVO:00000252](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000252)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;terminal moraine|Ridges of unconsolidated debris deposited at the snout or end of the glacier. They usually reflect the shape of the glacier's terminus.|

|[ENVO:01001177](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001177)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;arable land|Land which is regularly manipulated by human activities, such as plowing or tilling, in order to grow crops.|
|[ENVO:01001178](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001178)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pasturable land|Land which hosts a community of herbaceous plants - such as grasses and forbs - upon which animals may graze.|

|[ENVO:00000279](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000279)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;saline pan|A flat expanse of ground covered with salt and other minerals, usually shining white under the sun. A salt pan is formed where water pools. A saline pan would be a lake or a pond if it were located in a climate where the rate of water evaporation were not faster than the rate of water precipitation, i.e., if it were not in a desert. If the water is unable to drain into the ground, it remains on the surface until it evaporates, leaving behind whatever minerals were dissolved. Over thousands of years, the minerals (usually salts) accumulate on the surface.|

|[ENVO:01000261](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000261)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lysocline|A layer within a marine water body where the rate of calcite dissolution changes rapidly with depth. The increase in the rate of calcite dissolution with depth is largely due to the concomitant fall in calcite saturation.|
|[ENVO:01000079](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000079)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine lysocline|The marine lysocline denotes the depth in the ocean below which the rate of dissolution of calcite increases dramatically. As water column depth and therefore pressure increases, the corresponding calcite saturation of seawater decreases and the calcite begins dissolve.|

|[ENVO:01000960](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000960)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;secondary atmosphere|A planetary atmosphere which has formed as a result of its planet's volcanic activity, or by accumulation of material from comet impacts.|

|[ENVO:01000543](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000543)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;atmospheric layer|A layer that is part of the atmosphere.|
|[ENVO:01000538](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000538)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;stratosphere|The layer of the atmosphere which is sandwiched between the troposphere and mesosphere. Of the energy that reaches the Earth from the sun, only 3% is absorbed in the stratosphere, but that includes the vitally important process of absorption of ultraviolet radiation by the stratospheric ozone layer. The stratosphere is cloudless and dust free, and almost unaffected by the turbulent conditions of the underlying level of the atmosphere. (Source: WRIGHT)|
|[ENVO:01000539](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000539)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mesosphere|The mesosphere is part of the earth's atmosphere which is between the stratosphere and the thermosphere in which temperature decreases with altitude to the atmosphere's absolute minimum|
|[ENVO:01000540](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000540)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;troposphere|The lowest of the concentric layers of the atmosphere, occurring between the Earth's surface and the tropopause. It is the zone where atmospheric turbulence is at its greatest and where the bulk of the Earth's weather is generated. It contains almost all the water vapour and aerosols and three-quarters of the total gaseous mass of the atmosphere. Throughout the troposphere temperature decreases with height at a mean rate of 6.5Â°C/km and the whole zone is capped by either an inversion of temperature or an isothermal layer at the tropopause. (Source: WHIT)|
|[ENVO:01000541](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000541)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thermosphere|The thermosphere is a part of the earth's atmosphere that begins at about 50 miles (80 kilometers) above the earth's surface, extends to outer space, and is characterized by steadily increasing temperature with height|
|[ENVO:01000542](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000542)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ozone layer|The ozone layer is a layer of gases in the stratosphere which contains high concentrations of ozone gas relative to other parts of the atmosphere.|
|[ENVO:01000545](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000545)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ionosphere|The ionosphere is a layer of the Earth's atmosphere which extends from about 60 to 1,000 kilometers above the planetary surface and is ionised by solar radiation. It includes the thermosphere and parts of the mesosphere and exosphere.|
|[ENVO:01000546](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000546)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exosphere|The exosphere is an atmospheric layer where molecules are gravitationally bound to a planetary body, but where their density is too low for them to behave as a gas by colliding with each other. In the case of bodies with substantial atmospheres, such as Earth's atmosphere, the exosphere is the uppermost layer, where the atmosphere thins out and merges with interplanetary space. It is located directly above the thermosphere.|
|[ENVO:01000544](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000544)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;boundary layer|A boundary layer is a layer of fluid in the immediate vicinity of a bounding surface where the effects of viscosity are significant enough to distort the surrounding non-viscous flow.|
|[ENVO:01000323](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000323)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;atmospheric boundary layer|The atmospheric boundary layer is the lowest layer of an atmosphere which is strongly influenced by its contact with a planetary surface with strong vertical mixing and in which physical quantities such as flow velocity, temperature, and moisture display rapid fluctuations (turbulence).|
|[ENVO:01000639](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000639)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;planetary structural layer|A planetary structural layer is laminar part of a terrestrial planet or other rocky body large enough to have differentiation by density. Planetary layers have differing physicochemical properties and composition.|
|[ENVO:01000638](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000638)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;planetary crust|A planetary crust is the outermost solid shell of a rocky planet or natural satellite, which is chemically distinct from the underlying mantle.|
|[ENVO:01000640](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000640)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;planetary mantle|A planetary mantle is a planetary layer which is an interior part of a terrestrial planet or other rocky body large enough to have differentiation by density.|
|[ENVO:01000641](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000641)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;planetary core|A planetary core is the innermost structural layer or layers of a planet. The core may be entirely liquid, entirely solid, or have both liquid and solid parts.|
|[ENVO:01000642](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000642)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;outer planetary core|outer planetary core|
|[ENVO:01000643](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000643)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inner planetary core|inner planetary core|
|[ENVO:01000644](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000644)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;liquid planetary core|A liquid planetary core is a planetary core which is primarily composed of liquid material.|
|[ENVO:01000645](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000645)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;solid planetary core|A solid planetary core is a planetary core which is primarily composed of solid material.|
|[ENVO:01000646](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000646)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lithosphere|A lithosphere is the outermost shell of a terrestrial-type planet or natural satellite that is defined by its rigid mechanical properties.|
|[ENVO:01000647](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000647)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;asthenosphere|An asthenosphere is a layer of a terrestrial-type planet or natural satellite which is highly viscous, mechanically weak, and ductilely deforming.|
|[ENVO:01000748](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000748)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continental crust|A layer of igneous, sedimentary, and metamorphic rocks that forms continents and the areas of shallow seabed close to their shores, known as continental shelves.|
|[ENVO:01000749](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000749)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;oceanic crust|Oceanic crust is the uppermost layer of the oceanic portion of a tectonic plate.|
|[ENVO:01000750](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000750)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Mohorovicic discontinuity|The Mohorovicic discontinuity, usually referred to as the Moho, is the boundary between the Earth's crust and the mantle, indicating a change in composition.|
|[ENVO:01001273](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001273)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;liquid layer|A layer which is primarily composed of some liquid material.|
|[ENVO:01000325](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000325)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aquatic layer|A layer in a water mass, itself composed primarily of water.|
|[ENVO:00000038](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000038)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lagoon|A sheet of saline water separated from the open sea by sand or shingle banks. The sheet of water between an offshore reef, especially of coral and mainland. The sheet of water within a ring or horseshoe shaped atoll.|
|[ENVO:01000080](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000080)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pelagic isothermal surface|A roughly planar, pelagic region characterised by equal water temperature.|
|[ENVO:01000081](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000081)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pelagic isohaline surface|A roughly planar, pelagic region characterised by equal salinity.|
|[ENVO:01000083](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000083)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pelagic isopycnal surface|A roughly planar, pelagic region characterised by equal water density.|
|[ENVO:01000283](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000283)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lake layer|A layer which is part of a lake.|
|[ENVO:00002130](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00002130)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hypolimnion|The dense, bottom layer of water in a thermally-stratified lake. It is the layer that lies below the thermocline.|
|[ENVO:00002131](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00002131)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;epilimnion|The top-most layer in a thermally stratified lake, occurring above the deeper hypolimnion. It is warmer and typically has a higher pH and dissolved oxygen concentration than the hypolimnion.|
|[ENVO:01000295](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000295)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine layer|A layer that is part of a marine water body.|
|[ENVO:00000206](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000206)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine neritic zone|The water mass of an ocean directly above a continental shelf.|
|[ENVO:00000207](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000207)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;oceanic zone|The water mass of an ocean that is not above a continental shelf.|
|[ENVO:00000208](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000208)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine pelagic zone|An open ocean region.|
|[ENVO:00000209](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000209)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine photic zone|The zone of an ocean from the surface to where photosynthesis can occur, due to the penetration of light.|
|[ENVO:00000210](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000210)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine aphotic zone|The zone of an ocean below 200m, in which photosynthesis cannot occur due to the lack of light.|
|[ENVO:00000211](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000211)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine bathypelagic zone|The one of an ocean below the 10degC thermocline down to a temperature of 4degC.|
|[ENVO:00000212](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000212)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine abyssalpelagic zone|The zone of the ocean below the bathypelagic zone, with its lowest boundary at about 6000m.|
|[ENVO:00000213](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000213)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine mesopelagic zone|The zone of an ocean immediately below the photic zone down to a depth where the water temperature is 10degC (the thermocline).|
|[ENVO:00000214](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000214)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hadalpelagic zone|The zone of an ocean in oceanic trenches, lying between 6000m and 10,000m.|
|[ENVO:01000061](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000061)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine wind mixed layer|The upper part of the marine water column with generally uniform properties resulting from wind-driven mixing.|
|[ENVO:01001581](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001581)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sea surface layer|A surface layer of a water body which is part of an ocean or sea.|
|[ENVO:01000326](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000326)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deep chlorophyll maximum layer|A subsurface layer in a water body, typically an ocean or lake, in which chlorophyll concentrations reach their maximum.|
|[ENVO:01000862](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000862)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;turbulent aquatic surface layer|A turbulent surface layer of a water body maintained by strong currents setting over submerged ridges or shoals or by winds opposing a current.|
|[ENVO:01001191](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001191)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;water surface|The surface layer of a volume of water.|
|[ENVO:01001554](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001554)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;surface layer of a water body|A water surface that is part of a water body.|
|[ENVO:01001551](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001551)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ice lead|A surface layer of a water body which has been formed as the result of surface ice fracturing and moving apart.|
|[ENVO:01001550](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001550)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sea-ice lead|An ice lead which occurs in a marine water body and is bounded by sea ice.|
|[ENVO:01001552](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001552)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;flaw lead|An ice lead between a mass of fast ice and a mass of pack ice.|
|[ENVO:01001553](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001553)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shore lead|An ice lead which occurs between the shore and pack ice.|
|[ENVO:01001555](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001555)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;frozen lead|An ice lead within which new, nilas, and young ice has formed.|

|[ENVO:01001301](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001301)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aquatic estuarine layer|A layer of liquid that is part of an estuary.|

|[ENVO:01001324](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001324)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine tidal riverine coastal pycnocline|An estuarine coastal pycnocline which is composed primarily of fresh tidal water.|
|[ENVO:01001314](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001314)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine coastal lower water column|A layer of estuarine water which extends from an estuarine pycnocline or mid-depth to the estuarine bed and from the shore to a fiat boundary where the estuary bed below the water column reaches a depth of 4 meters.|
|[ENVO:01001325](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001325)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine tidal riverine coastal lower water column|A layer of fresh estuarine water which extends from an estuarine pycnocline or mid-depth to the estuarine bed and from the land-water interface to a fiat boundary where the estuary bed below the water column reaches a depth of 4 meters.|
|[ENVO:01001315](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001315)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine open water surface layer|A layer of estuarine water which extends a few centimeters from the surface of the water column towards the estuary bed and from a fiat boundary where the estuary bed below the water column reaches a depth of 4 meters until the end of the estuary most distal from the coast.|
|[ENVO:01001326](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001326)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine tidal riverine open water surface layer|A layer of fresh estuarine water which extends a few centimeters from the surface of the water column towards the estuary bed and from a fiat boundary where the estuary bed below the water column reaches a depth of 4 meters until the end of the estuary most distal from the coast.|
|[ENVO:01001316](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001316)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;estuarine open water upper water column|A layer of estuarine water which extends from the surface of the water column to the pycnocline or mid-depth and from a fiat boundary where the estuary bed below the water column reaches a depth of 4 meters until the end of the estuary most distal from the coast.|

|[ENVO:00000279](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000279)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;saline pan|A flat expanse of ground covered with salt and other minerals, usually shining white under the sun. A salt pan is formed where water pools. A saline pan would be a lake or a pond if it were located in a climate where the rate of water evaporation were not faster than the rate of water precipitation, i.e., if it were not in a desert. If the water is unable to drain into the ground, it remains on the surface until it evaporates, leaving behind whatever minerals were dissolved. Over thousands of years, the minerals (usually salts) accumulate on the surface.|

|[ENVO:01000909](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000909)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;biocrust|A surface layer of a solid environmental material which is formed by the presence and activity of photosynthetic microbial assemblages colonising it.|
|[ENVO:01000910](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000910)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;soil biocrust|A biocrust which is formed by photosynthetic microbial assemblages colonising the surface layer of a portion of arid soil. Through their successional dynamics, these communities reduce the soil surface's albedo, impart it with stability against erosion, modify its hydrology, and promote its fertility.|
|[ENVO:01001181](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001181)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rhizoplane|A surface layer which is composed of the external surface of a root, together with closely adhering soil particles and debris|
|[ENVO:01001271](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001271)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;impermeable surface layer|A surface layer through which liquids or gases cannot pass.|

|[ENVO:01001503](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001503)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;glacial surface layer|A solid surface layer which is that part of a glacier in contact with a planetary atmosphere.|

|[ENVO:01001543](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001543)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;water ice surface layer|An ice surface layer which is primarily composed of water ice.|
|[ENVO:01001559](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001559)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cryopeg|A layer which is composed of ground that 1) remains unfrozen due to increased solute concentration and 2) is present within a mass of permafrost.|
|[ENVO:01000299](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000299)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Taylor column|A Taylor column is a column of deflected fluid flow which is formed in a perturbed, rotating fluid, is parallel to the axis of rotation, and extends above the obstacle perturbing the fluid in a rigid manner.|
|[ENVO:01000072](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000072)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;marine Taylor column|A marine Taylor column is a Taylor column that is formed in a marine body of water. Currents flowing over shoaling topography such as seamounts are accelerated and destabilised, resulting in Taylor columns. Eddies and internal waves are generated downstream of the topological feature and may extend 1000 m or so above them. This may result in a localised increase in primary production where the Taylor column reaches surface waters.|
|[ENVO:01000300](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000300)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;atmospheric Taylor column|An atmospheric Taylor column is a Taylor column that is formed in the atmosphere. Atmospheric Taylor columns often form above islands resulting in vortex streets in the atmosphere.|
|[ENVO:01000443](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000443)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;salt mass|An accumulation of a salt, typically sodium chloride.|
|[ENVO:01000450](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000450)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;salt glacier|A mass of salt which has erupted onto a planetary surface, usually through sedimentary rock.|
|[ENVO:01000505](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000505)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;salt dome|A dome-shaped mass of salt formed when a thick bed of evaporite minerals (mainly salt, or halite) found at depth intrudes vertically into surrounding rock strata, forming a diapir.|
|[ENVO:01001109](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01001109)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Karman vortex street|A succession of swirling vortices caused by the unsteady separation of flow of a fluid around one or more blunt bodies.|
|[ENVO:00000094](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000094)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic feature|A part of an astronomical body associated with a volcano - an opening, or rupture, in that body's surface or crust - which allows hot, molten rock, ash and gases to escape from deep below the surface.|
|[ENVO:00000096](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000096)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;caldera|A feature formed by the collapse of land following a volcanic eruption.|
|[ENVO:00000222](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000222)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;oceanic island|An island that does not sit on a continental shelf, and is of volcanic origin.|
|[ENVO:00000166](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000166)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;atoll|An oceanic island, often having a characteristic ring-like shape surrounding a lagoon. Atolls are formed when coral reef grows around a volcanic island that later subsides into the ocean.|
|[ENVO:00000246](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000246)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic crater|A crater formed by a volcano, within which occurs a vent (or vents) from which magma erupts as gases, lava, and ejecta.|
|[ENVO:00000247](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000247)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcano|An opening, or rupture, in the Earth's surface or crust, which allows hot, molten rock, ash and gases to escape from deep below the surface.|
|[ENVO:00000350](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000350)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;somma volcano|A volcanic caldera that has been partially filled by a new central cone.|
|[ENVO:00000370](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000370)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tuya|A distinctive, flat-topped, steep-sided volcano formed when lava erupts through a thick glacier or ice sheet.|
|[ENVO:00000371](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000371)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;complex volcano|A volcano with more than one feature. They form because changes of their eruptive characteristics or the location of multiple vents in an area. Stratovolcanoes may form complex volcanoes, because they may overlap another from explosive eruptions, lava flows, pyroclastic flows and by repeated eruptions, to make multiple summits and vents. Stratovolcanoes could also form a large caldera that gets filled in by multiple small cinder cones, lava domes and craters may also develop on the caldera's rim.|
|[ENVO:00000402](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000402)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mud volcano|A volcano created by geologically excreted liquids and gases, although there are several different processes which may cause such activity. Temperatures are much cooler than igneous processes.|
|[ENVO:00000403](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000403)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shield volcano|A large volcano with shallowly-sloping sides.|
|[ENVO:00000372](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000372)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pyroclastic shield volcano|A shield volcano that is formed mostly of pyroclastic and highly explosive eruptions rather than relatively fluid basaltic lava issuing from vents or fissures on the surface of the volcano. They typically display low-angle flank slopes and have little or no central collapse, although a shallow sag in the shield is commonly observed. Lava is commonly extruded after the cessation of explosive activity commonly superposes the vent region.|
|[ENVO:00000404](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000404)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;stratovolcano|A tall, conical volcano composed of many layers of hardened lava, tephra, and volcanic ash. These volcanoes are characterized by a steep profile and periodic, explosive eruptions. The lava that flows from them is viscous, and cools and hardens before spreading very far. The source magma of this rock is classified as acidic, or high in silica to intermediate (rhyolite, dacite, or andesite).|
|[ENVO:00000407](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000407)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;subglacial volcano|A volcano produced by subglacial eruptions or eruptions beneath the surface of a lake melted into a glacier or ice mass by the rising lava.|
|[ENVO:00000408](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000408)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic fissure|A linear volcanic vent through which lava erupts, usually without any explosive activity. The vent is usually a few meters wide and may be many kilometers long. Fissure vents can cause large flood basalts and hannels. The volcano can usually be seen as a crack in the ground or on the ocean floor. Narrow fissures can be filled in with lava that hardens.|
|[ENVO:01000439](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000439)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;andesitic volcano|andesitic volcano|
|[ENVO:01000440](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000440)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dacitic volcano|dacitic volcano|
|[ENVO:00000351](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000351)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic arc|A chain of volcanic islands or mountains formed by plate tectonics as an oceanic tectonic plate subducts under another tectonic plate and produces magma.|
|[ENVO:00000352](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000352)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continental arc|A volcanic arc formed by the subduction of oceanic crust below continental crust.|
|[ENVO:00000353](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000353)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;island arc|A volcanic arc formed by the subduction of oceanic crust other oceanic crust on an adjacent tectonic plate.|
|[ENVO:00000398](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000398)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic cone|Built by fragments (called ejecta) thrown up (ejected) from a volcanic vent, piling up around the vent in the shape of a cone with a central crater.|
|[ENVO:00000356](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000356)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pyroclastic cone|A cone made of material ejected from a volcano. The material can range from finest particles. In comparison, cinder cones are more uniform. They are usually found in or on larger features, such as stratovolcanoes, shield volcanoes and can be found inside calderas, however they can also be an independent feature. They can range from a few metres in height and are usually formed by a single eruption.|
|[ENVO:00000399](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000399)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ash cone|A cone that is composed of particles of silt to sand size. Explosive eruptions from a vent where the magma is interacting with groundwater or the sea (as in an eruption off the coast) produce steam and are called phreatic. The interaction between the magma, expanding steam, and volcanic gases results in the ejection of mostly small particles called ash. Fallen ash has the consistency of flour. The unconsolidated ash forms an ash cone which becomes a tuff cone or tuff ring once the ash consolidates.|
|[ENVO:00000400](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000400)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cinder cone|A cone built almost entirely of loose volcanic fragments called cinders (pumice, pyroclastics, or tephra). They are built from particles and blobs of congealed lava ejected from a single vent. As the gas-charged lava is blown violently into the air, it breaks into small fragments that solidify and fall as cinders around the vent to form a circular or oval cone. Most cinder cones have a bowl-shaped crater at the summit.|
|[ENVO:00000401](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000401)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;spatter cone|A volcanic cone formed of molten lava ejected from a vent somewhat like taffy. Expanding gases in the lava fountains tear the liquid rock into irregular gobs that fall back to earth, forming a heap around the vent. The still partly liquid rock splashed down and over the sides of the developing mound is called spatter. Because spatter is not fully solid when it lands, the individual deposits are very irregular in shape and weld together as they cool, and in this way particularly differ from cinder and ash.|
|[ENVO:01000664](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000664)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tuff cone|A cone that is composed of consolidated volcanic ash.|
|[ENVO:00000498](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000498)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;volcanic dike|An intrusive igneous body. Its thickness is usually much smaller than its other two dimensions. Thickness can vary from sub-centimeter scale to many meters in thickness and the lateral dimensions can extend over many kilometers. A dike is an intrusion into a cross-cutting fissure, meaning a dike cuts across other pre-existing layers or bodies of rock, this means that a dike is always younger than the rocks that contain it. Dikes are usually high angle to near vertical in orientation, but subsequent tectonic deformation may rotate the sequence of strata through which the dike lies so that the latter becomes horizontal.|
|[ENVO:01000438](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000438)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lava flow|A lava flow is a moving outpouring of lava, which is created during a non-explosive effusive eruption.|
|[ENVO:01000731](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:01000731)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;igneous extrusion|A mass of igneous rock formed when hot magma flows out (extrudes) onto a planetary surface as lava or explodes violently into the atmosphere to fall back as pyroclastics or tuff.|
|[ENVO:00000191](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000191)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;solid astronomical body part|A part of an astronomical body which is primarily composed of a continuous volume of solid material, shaped by one or more environmental processes.|
|[ENVO:00000013](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000013)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cave system|A collection of caves interconnected by enterable passages or linked hydrologically or a cave with an extensive complex of chambers and passages.|
|[ENVO:00000067](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000067)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cave|Naturally formed, subterranean open area or chamber.|
|[ENVO:00000001](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000001)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bedding-plane cave|A cavity developed along a bedding-plane and elongate in cross-section as a result.|
|[ENVO:00000030](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000030)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dead cave|A cave without streams or drips of water.|
|[ENVO:00000071](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000071)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fault cave|A cave developed along a fault or fault zone, either by movement of the fault or by preferential solution along it.|
|[ENVO:00000263](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000263)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fissure cave|A narrow, vertical cave passage, often developed along a joint but not necessarily so. Usually due to solution but sometimes to tension.|
|[ENVO:00000321](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000321)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;joint-plane cave|A cavity developed along a joint and elongate in cross-section.|

|[ENVO:00000259](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000259)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lacustrine plain|A plain that originally formed in a lacustrine environment, that is, as the bed of a lake, but from which the water has disappeared, by natural drainage, evaporation or other geophysical processes.|
|[ENVO:00000312](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000312)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sandur|The plain formed by the large amounts of silt and sediment, picked up as a glacier erodes the underlying rocks as it moves slowly downhill, and at the snout of the glacier, meltwater can carry this sediment away from the glacier and deposit it on a broad plain. The material in the outwash plain is often size-sorted by the water runoff of the melting glacier with the finest materials, like silt, being the most distantly re-deposited, whereas larger boulders are the closest to the original terminus of the glacier.|
|[ENVO:00000434](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000434)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;outwash fan|A fan-shaped body of sediments deposited by braided streams from a melting glacier.|

|[ENVO:00000175](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000175)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;karst|A feature shaped by the dissolution of a soluble layer or layers of bedrock, usually carbonate rock such as limestone or dolomite. These landscapes display distinctive surface features and underground drainages, and in some examples there may be little or no surface drainage.|
|[ENVO:00000333](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000333)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;subjacent karst|Karst developed in soluble beds underlying other rock formations; the surface may or may not be affected by the karst development.|
|[ENVO:00000334](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000334)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;syngenetic karst|Karst developed in eolian calcarenite when the development of karst features has taken place at the same time as the lithification of dune sand.|
|[ENVO:00000335](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000335)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;polygonal karst|Karst completely pitted by closed depressions so that divides between them form a crudely polygonal network.|
|[ENVO:00000336](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000336)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doline karst|Karst dominated by closed depressions, chiefly dolines, perforating a simple surface.|

|[ENVO:00000283](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000283)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ridge|A long and narrow elevation with steep sides.|
|[ENVO:00000282](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000282)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;esker|A long, winding ridge of stratified sand and gravel which occur in glaciated and formerly glaciated regions of Europe and North America.|
|[ENVO:00000429](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000429)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;arete|A thin, almost knife-like, ridge of rock which is typically formed when two glaciers erode parallel U-shaped valleys. The arte is a thin ridge of rock that is left separating the two valleys. Artes can also form when two glacial cirques erode towards one another, although frequently this results in a saddle-shaped pass, called a col.|
|[ENVO:00000441](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000441)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;terracette|A ridge on a hillside formed when saturated soil particles expand, then contract as they dry, causing them to move slowly downhill.|
|[ENVO:00000528](https://narrative.kbase.us/#ontology/term/envo_ontology/ENVO:00000528)|&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ice cap ridge|A linear elevation on an icecap.|
